liii volterra -lrb- this letter be casually omit from its proper place near the beginning of the volume -rrb- rome _ April _ 15 1835 towards the end of march i go from pisa to volterra this you know be a very ancient city one of the stronghold of etrurium when rome be in its cradle and in more modern time in the age of italian republic large enough to form a independent community of considerable importance it be now a decayed town contain about four thousand inhabitant some of whom be family of the poor and proud nobility common enough over all italy who be say to quarrel with each other more fiercely in volterra than almost anywhere else it be the old feud of the montague and the capulet on a humbler scale and the dispute of the volterra nobility be the more violent and implacable for be hereditary poor creature too proud to engage in business too indolent for literature exclude from political employment by the nature of the government there be nothing leave for they but to starve intrigue and quarrel you may judge how miserably poor they be when you be tell they can not afford even to cultivate the favorite art of modern italy the art best suit to the genius of a soft and effeminate people there be i be tell but one pianoforte in the whole town and that be own by a florentine lady who have recently come to reside here for several mile before reach volterra we attention be fix by the extraordinary aspect of the country through which we be pass the road gradually ascend and we find ourselves among deep ravine and steep high broken bank principally of clay barren and in most place wholly bare of herbage a scene of complete desolation be it not for a cottage here and there perch upon the height a few sheep attend by a boy and a dog grazing on the brink of one of the precipice or a solitary patch of bright green wheat in some spot where the rain have not yet carry away the vegetable mould imagine to yourself a elevated country like the highland of pennsylvanium or the western part of massachusett imagine vast bed of loam and clay in place of the ledge of rock and then fancy the whole region to be tear by water-spout and torrent into gulley too profound to be pass with sharp ridge between -- strip of its tree and its grass -- and you will have some idea of the country near volterra i could not help fancy while i look at it that as the earth grow old the rib of rock which once uphold the mountain have become change into the bare heap of earth which i see about I that time and the element have destroy the cohesion of the particle of which they be form and that now the rain be sweep they down to the mediterranean to fill its bed and cause its water to encroach upon the land it be impossible for I to prevent the apprehension from pass through my mind that such might be the fate of other quarter of the globe in age yet to come that they rock must crumble and they mountain be level until the water shall again cover the face of the earth unless new mountain shall be throw up by eruption of internal fire they tell I in volterra that this frightful region have once be productive and under cultivation but that after a plague which four or five hundred year since have depopulate the country it be abandon and neglect and the rain have reduce it to its present state in the midst of this desolate tract which be however here and there intersperse with fertile spot rise the mountain on which volterra be situate where the inhabitant breathe a pure and keen atmosphere almost perpetually cool and only die of pleurisy and apoplexy while below on the bank of the cecina which in full sigjit wind its way to the sea they die of fever one of the ravine of which i have speak -- the _ balza _ they call it at volterra -- have plough a deep chasm on the north side of this mountain and be every year rapidly approach the city on its summit i stand on its edge and look down a bank of soft red earth five hundred foot in height a few rod in front of I i see where a road have cross the spot in which the gulf now yawn the track of the last year 's carriage be see reach to the edge on both side the ruin of a convent be close at hand the inmate of which two or three year since have be remove by the government to the town for safety these will soon be undermine by the advance chasm together with a fine piece of old etruscan wall once inclose the city build of enormous uncemented parallelogram of stone and look as if it might be the work of the giant who live before the flood a neighbor church will next fall into the gulf which finally if means be not take to prevent its progress will reach and sap the present wall of the city swallow up what time have so long spare a few hundred crown say a inhabitant of volterra to I would stop all this mischief a wall at the bottom of the chasm and a heap of branch of tree or other rubbish to check the fall of the earth be all that would be necessary i ask why these means be not use because he reply those to whom the charge of these matter belong will not take the trouble somebody must devise a plan for the purpose and somebody must take upon himself the labor of see it execute they find it easier to put it off the antiquity of volterra consist of a etruscan burial-ground in which the tomb still remain piece of the old and incredibly massive etruscan wall include a far larger circuit than the present city two etruscan gate of immemorial antiquity older doubtless than any thing at rome build of enormous stone one of they serve even yet as a entrance to the town and a multitude of cinerary vessel mostly of alabaster sculpture with numerous figure in _ alto relievo _ these figure be sometimes allegorical representation and sometimes embody the fable of the greek mythology among they be some in the most perfect style of grecian art the subject of which be take from the poem of homer group represent the besieger of troy and its defender or ulyss with he companion and he ship i gaze with exceed delight on these work of forget artist who have the verse of homer by heart -- work just draw from the tomb where they have be bury for thousand of year and look as if fresh from the chisel we have letter to the commandant of the fortress a ancient-looking stronghold build by the medicus family over which we be conduct by he adjutant a courteous gentleman with a red nose who walk as if keep time to military music from the summit of the tower we have a extensive and most remarkable prospect it be the 19th day of march and below we the side of the mountain scoop into irregular dell be cover with fruit-tree just break into leaf and flower beyond stretch the region of barrenness i have already describe to the west of which lay the green pasture of the maremma the air of which in summer be deadly and still further west be spread the water of the mediterranean out of which be see rise the mountain of corsica to the north and northeast be the appenine cap with snow embosome the fertile lower valley of the arno with the city of pisa and leghorn in sight to the south we trace the winding of the cecina and see ascend into the air the smoke of a hot-water lake agitate perpetually with the escape of gas which we be tell be visit by dante and from which he draw image for he description of hell some frenchman have now convert it into a borax manufactory the natural heat of the water serve to extract the salt the fortress be use as a prison for person guilty of offens against the state on the top of the tower we pass four prisoner of state well-dressed young man who appear to have be entertaining themselves with music have guitar and other instrument in they hand they salute the adjutant as he go by they who in return take off he hat they have be condemn for a conspiracy against the government the commandant give we a hospitable reception in show we the fortress he congratulate we that we have no occasion for such engine of
